Genome Biol.19, 127 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2733">9</a></sup>. There are also more gene duplication events in sweet cherry and flowering cherry (<i>P. yedoensis</i>) than in peach, almond, apricot, and Chinese plum. These results may explain why sweet cherry has a larger genome than other diploid <i>Prunus</i> species.</p><p>Two gene duplication events were identified in the genome of sweet cherry compared with peach v2.0, which were involved in the salicylic acid synthesis and salicylic acid signal transduction pathways. We also identified some auxin-responsive genes that were differentially expressed during the fruit development of sweet cherry. This finding suggests that auxin plays a complicated role in the fruit ripening process of sweet cherry. Our well-assembled reference genome of sweet cherry cv. Tieton will support studies on gene function characterization and benefit the research community in the future.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec11" data-title="Materials and methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec11-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec11">Materials and methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec11-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">DNA extraction and sequencing</h3><p>Leaf samples from sweet cherry cv. Tieton grown in the experimental orchard of Shandong Institute of Pomology, Taian, China, were collected and frozen in liquid nitrogen. Genomic DNA (gDNA) was extracted, size selected and sequenced on an Oxford Nanopore PromethION system by BioMarker Technology Co., Ltd. (Beijing, China). Low-quality reads, reads with adapters and reads shorter than 2000ânt were filtered out. Before assembly, 2000 reads were randomly selected and subjected to BLAST searches against the NT database using BLAST v2.9.0+, and no obvious external contamination was found. For Illumina sequencing, a paired-end library with an insert size of 350âbp was constructed and sequenced by CapitalBio Technology Inc. (Beijing, China) in accordance with the manufacturerâs protocol using the Illumina HiSeq X Ten platform with a 150-nt layout. A total of 48.27âGb of Illumina raw sequencing data was generated for the survey, correction and evaluation of the genome.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec13">Genome assembly</h3><p>Several approaches were applied to assemble the sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome using MaSuRCA v3.3.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Zimin, A. V. et al. The MaSuRCA genome assembler. Bioinformatics29, 2669â2677 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2766">40</a></sup>, Canu v1.8<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Koren, S. et al. Canu: scalable and accurate long-read assembly via adaptive k-mer weighting and repeat separation. Genome Res.27, 722â736 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2770">41</a></sup>, wtdbg2 v2.5, and NECAT v0.01<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Chen, Y. et al. Fast and accurate assembly of Nanopore reads via progressive error correction and adaptive read selection. bioRxiv.&#xA;&#xA;https://doi.org/10.1101/2020.02.01.930107&#xA;&#xA; (2020)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2774">42</a></sup>. To facilitate reading, a complete set of parameters for each tool is listed in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#MOESM1">S11</a>. BUSCO v3.0.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Waterhouse, R. M. et al. BUSCO applications from quality assessments to gene prediction and phylogenomics. Mol. Biol. Evol35, 543â548 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2781">43</a></sup> was used to assess all the assemblies. The preliminary assemblies of Canu, wtdbg2, and NECAT were first polished with medaka (<a href="https://github.com/nanoporetech/medaka">https://github.com/nanoporetech/medaka</a>) using Nanopore long reads and then polished three times with NextPolish v1.0.5 using Illumina short reads. The three draft assemblies were subsequently processed with Purge Haplotigs v1.1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Roach, M. J., Schmidt, S. A. &amp; Borneman, A. R. Purge Haplotigs: allelic contig reassignment for third-gen diploid genome assemblies. BMC Bioinforma.19, 460 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2793">44</a></sup> to investigate the proper assignment of contigs.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Hi-C analysis and pseudochromosome construction</h3><p>Fresh young leaves collected from a sweet cherry cv. Tieton tree were fixed using formaldehyde at a concentration of 1%. The chromatin was cross-linked and digested using the restriction enzyme HindIII. The 5â² overhangs were labeled with a biotinylated tag and end repaired. After ligation, the DNA was extracted, sheared, and subjected to selection for fragments with lengths between 300 and 700âbp. The biotin-containing fragments were captured for library construction. Finally, the quality of the purified library was evaluated with a Qubit 3.0 fluorometer (Thermo Fisher Scientific, Inc.), quantitative PCR (qPCR), and an Agilent 2100 instrument. The qualified library was sequenced using the Illumina HiSeq X Ten platform with a 150-bp PE layout. To obtain the unique mapped read pairs, we first truncated the paired reads at the putative Hi-C junctions and then aligned them to the sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome assembly using the Arima-HiC Mapping Pipeline (<a href="https://github.com/ArimaGenomics/mapping_pipeline">https://github.com/ArimaGenomics/mapping_pipeline</a>). We then used the partition, rescue, optimize, and build functions of the ALLHiC v0.9.12<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Zhang, X., Zhang, S., Zhao, Q., Ming, R. &amp; Tang, H. Assembly of allele-aware, chromosomal-scale autopolyploid genomes based on Hi-C data. Nat. Plants5, 833â845 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2812">14</a></sup> pipeline to construct the chromosomal-level scaffolds of the sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome. After ALLHiC scaffolding, pseudomolecules and Hi-C contact maps were built by using Juicer v1.6.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Durand, N. C. et al. Juicer provides a one-click system for analyzing loop-resolution Hi-C experiments. Cell Syst.3, 95â98 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2816">45</a></sup> and the 3D de novo assembly pipeline v180114<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Dudchenko, O. et al. De novo assembly of the Aedes aegypti genome using Hi-C yields chromosome-length scaffolds. Science356, 92â95 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2820">46</a></sup>. Juicebox Assembly Tools v1.9.8 were used to visualize and manually correct the large-scale inversions and translocations to obtain the final pseudochromosomes.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Genome assembly quality evaluation</h3><p>Following the approach of Ou et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Ou, S., Chen, J. &amp; Jiang, N. Assessing genome assembly quality using the LTR Assembly Index (LAI). Nucleic Acids Res.46, e126 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2832">15</a></sup>, LTRharvest v1.6.1 and LTR_retriever v2.8 were first used to detect LTR-RTs in the genome assemblies, and then the LAIs of each genome were calculated using LTR_retriever. The genome size of sweet cherry cv. Tieton was estimated by using Jellyfish v2.2.10<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Marcais, G. &amp; Kingsford, C. A fast, lock-free approach for efficient parallel counting of occurrences of k-mers. Bioinformatics27, 764â770 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2836">47</a></sup> and GenomeScope v1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Vurture, G. W. et al. GenomeScope: fast reference-free genome profiling from short reads. Bioinformatics33, 2202â2204 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2840">48</a></sup> based on a k-mer counting method.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Repetitive sequence annotation</h3><p>RepeatModeler v.2.0.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Flynn, J. M. et al. RepeatModeler2: automated genomic discovery of transposable element families. bioRxiv. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.1101/856591&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2853">49</a></sup> was applied as the de novo method to identify repetitive elements in the sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome. Then, the homology-based tool RepeatMasker v.4.0.9<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Tarailo-Graovac, M. &amp; Chen, N. Using RepeatMasker to identify repetitive elements in genomic sequences. Curr. Protoc. Bioinformatics25, Unit 4â10 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2857">50</a></sup> was applied against Dfam v3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Hubley, R. et al. The Dfam database of repetitive DNA families. Nucleic Acids Res.44, D81âD89 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2861">51</a></sup> and Repbase library v20170127 using the Embryophyta settings.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Noncoding RNA prediction</h3><p>Infernal v1.1.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics29, 2933â2935 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2873">52</a></sup> was used to identify noncoding RNAs (ncRNAs) in the sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome by comparison with the RFAM database v14.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Kalvari, I. et al. Non-coding RNA analysis using the Rfam database. Curr. Protoc. Bioinforma.62, e51 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2877">53</a></sup>. tRNAscan-SE v2.0.5 was used to identify tRNAs. RNAmmer v1.1.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Lagesen, K. et al. RNAmmer: consistent and rapid annotation of ribosomal RNA genes. Nucleic Acids Res.35, 3100â3108 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2881">54</a></sup> was used to search for rRNAs. The results of the three pipelines were combined, and the overlapping annotations were removed.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Protein-coding gene prediction and functional annotation</h3><p>Funannotate v1.7.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Love, J. et al. nextgenusfs/funannotate: funannotate v1.7.2. Zenodo. &#xA;https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.3594559&#xA;&#xA; (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2893">55</a></sup>, which employs GeneMark-ES v4.48_3.60_lic<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Lomsadze, A., Ter-Hovhannisyan, V., Chernoff, Y. O. &amp; Borodovsky, M. Gene identification in novel eukaryotic genomes by self-training algorithm. Nucleic Acids Res.33, 6494â506 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2897">56</a></sup>, Augustus v3.3.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Hoff, K. J. &amp; Stanke, M. Predicting genes in single genomes with AUGUSTUS. Curr. Protoc. Bioinforma.65, e57 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2901">57</a></sup>, CodingQuarry v2.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Testa, A. C., Hane, J. K., Ellwood, S. R. &amp; Oliver, R. P. CodingQuarry: highly accurate hidden Markov model gene prediction in fungal genomes using RNA-seq transcripts. BMC Genomics.16, 170 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2905">58</a></sup>, SNAP v2006-07-28<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Korf, I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinforma.5, 59 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2909">59</a></sup>, and GlimmerHMM v3.0.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Majoros, W. H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics20, 2878â2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2914">60</a></sup>, was used to perform protein-coding gene prediction in the repeat-masked sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome. Briefly, we first trained the gene prediction model using our previously published transcript sequencing data for cv. Tieton fruit<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Wei, H. et al. Comparative transcriptome analysis of genes involved in anthocyanin biosynthesis in the red and yellow fruits of sweet cherry (Prunus avium L.). PLoS ONE10, e0121164 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2918">32</a></sup>. Then, protein-coding genes were predicted for the whole genome using the Funannotate prediction pipeline. All the predicted gene models, transcript alignments generated by PASA v2.4.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res.31, 5654â5666 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2922">61</a></sup>, and protein sequences of the peach v2.0 annotation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Verde, I. et al. The Peach v2.0 release: high-resolution linkage mapping and deep resequencing improve chromosome-scale assembly and contiguity. BMC Genomics.18, 225 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2926">6</a></sup> were input into EVidenceModeler v1.1.1 to obtain the final prediction of gene models for the sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome. The statistics of the prediction results and the weights used for EVidenceModeler are shown in Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#MOESM1">S12</a>. InterProScan5 v5.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics30, 1236â1240 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2933">62</a></sup> was used to annotate the predicted proteins against the InterPro database v77.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Mitchell, A. L. et al. InterPro in 2019: improving coverage, classification and access to protein sequence annotations. Nucleic Acids Res.47, D351âD360 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2938">63</a></sup>. EggNOG-mapper v1.0.3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Huerta-Cepas, J. et al. Fast genome-wide functional annotation through orthology assignment by eggNOG-Mapper. Mol. Biol. Evol.34, 2115â2122 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2942">17</a></sup> was used locally against emapperdb v4.5.1 for fast functional annotation with Gene Ontology<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Harris, M. A. et al. The Gene Ontology (GO) database and informatics resource. Nucleic Acids Res.32, D258âD261 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2946">21</a></sup> and COG functional categories<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Koonin, E. V. et al. A comprehensive evolutionary classification of proteins encoded in complete eukaryotic genomes. Genome Biol.5, R7 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2950">22</a></sup>. KAAS (KEGG Automatic Annotation Server)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Moriya, Y., Itoh, M., Okuda, S., Yoshizawa, A. C. &amp; Kanehisa, M. KAAS: an automatic genome annotation and pathway reconstruction server. Nucleic Acids Res.35, W182âW185 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2954">64</a></sup> was used to annotate the predicted protein sequences according to KEGG Orthology. The results of the InterProScan, EggNOG-mapper, and KEGG Orthology analyses were combined and fitted to the Funannotate annotation pipeline. UTRs were added by the Funannotate update pipeline using the transcript data.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">Gene orthologs and gene family analysis</h3><p>Gene orthologs and gene duplication events in the sweet cherry genome compared with the genomes of other <i>Prunus</i> plants were identified by OrthoFinder v2.3.11<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Emms, D. M. &amp; Kelly, S. OrthoFinder: phylogenetic orthology inference for comparative genomics. Genome Biol.20, 238 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2969">65</a></sup>. The GO enrichment analysis of these proteins was performed by using WEGO v2.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Ye, J. et al. WEGO 2.0: a web tool for analyzing and plotting GO annotations, 2018 update. Nucleic Acids Res.46, W71âW75 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2973">66</a></sup>. CAFÃ v4.21<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Han, M. V., Thomas, G. W., Lugo-Martinez, J. &amp; Hahn, M. W. Estimating gene gain and loss rates in the presence of error in genome assembly and annotation using CAFE 3. Mol. Biol. Evol.30, 1987â1997 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2977">67</a></sup> was employed to explore gene family size expansion and contraction following the provided protocol.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">RNAseq analysis and KEGG pathway enrichment of DEGs</h3><p>RNAseq analysis was performed following the protocol of Thomas W. Battaglia (<a href="https://github.com/twbattaglia/RNAseq-workflow">https://github.com/twbattaglia/RNAseq-workflow</a>). TCC-GUI was used to normalize the expression data and detect the DEGs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Su, W., Sun, J., Shimizu, K. &amp; Kadota, K. TCC-GUI: a Shiny-based application for differential expression analysis of RNA-Seq count data. BMC Res Notes12, 133 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d37401e2996">68</a></sup>. KOBAS 3.0 was used to perform the KEGG enrichment analysis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Xie, C. et al. KOBAS 2.0: a web server for annotation and identification of enriched pathways and diseases. Nucleic Acids Res.39, W316âW322 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d37401e3000">69</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec21">Genome synteny analysis</h3><p>A Python version of MCscan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Tang, H. et al. Synteny and collinearity in plant genomes. Science320, 486â488 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d37401e3012">70</a></sup> was employed to analyze the synteny between the sweet cherry cv. Tieton genome and the cv. Satonishiki genome or other genomes within <i>Prunus</i> following the approach of Haibao Tang. Circos v0.69-8<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Krzywinski, M. et al. Circos: an information aesthetic for comparative genomics. Genome Res.19, 1639â1645 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d37401e3019">71</a></sup> was used to generate the synteny plot between sweet cherry cv. Tieton and cv. Satonishiki.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>Raw sequencing reads have been deposited in the NCBI SRA (Sequence Read Archive) database under BioSample accession number SAMN13640536. This whole-genome shotgun project has been deposited in GenBank under the accession JAAOZG000000000. The version described in this paper is version JAAOZG010000000.</p>

                <h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="FPar1">Conflict of interest</h3>
                <p>The authors declare that they have no conflict of interest.</p>

                    <i>Hortic Res</i> <b>7, </b>122 (2020). https://doi.org/10.1038/s41438-020-00343-8</p><p class="c-bibliographic-information__download-citation u-hide-print"><a data-test="citation-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="download article citation" data-track-label="link" data-track-external="" href="/articles/s41438-020-00343-8.ris">Download citation<svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-download"></use></svg></a></p><ul class="c-bibliographic-information__list" data-test="publication-history"><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Received<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2020-03-26">26 March 2020</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Revised<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2020-04-29">29 April 2020</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Accepted<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2020-05-12">12 May 2020</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Published<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2020-08-01">01 August 2020</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item c-bibliographic-information__list-item--doi"><p><abbr title="Digital Object Identifier">DOI</abbr><span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1038/s41438-020-00343-8" data-track="click" data-track-action="view doi" data-track-label="link" itemprop="sameAs">https://doi.org/10.1038/s41438-020-00343-8</a></span></p></li></ul><div data-component="share-box"></div><div data-component="article-info-list"></div></div></div></div></div></section>
